<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Reese Witherspoon</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Laura Jeanne Reese Witherspoon</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iː</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="/ð/ 'th' in 'thy'">ð</span><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'">ər</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/uː/ long 'oo' in 'food'">uː</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born March 22, 1976) is an American actress and producer. Born in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge" title="Baton Rouge">Baton Rouge</a>, Louisiana and raised in <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, Witherspoon began her career as a child actress, making her professional screen debut in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_in_the_Moon" title="The Man in the Moon">The Man in the Moon</a></i> (1991), for which she was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Young_Artist_Award" title="Young Artist Award">Young Artist Award</a>.</p>
<p>Following breakout roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Desperate_Choices:_To_Save_My_Child" title="Desperate Choices: To Save My Child">Desperate Choices: To Save My Child</a></i> (1992) and <i><a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Bear" title="Jack the Bear">Jack the Bear</a></i>, she starred in the comedy-drama <i><a href="/wiki/Pleasantville_(film)" title="Pleasantville (film)">Pleasantville</a></i> (1998), for which she won the <a href="/wiki/Young_Hollywood_Awards" title="Young Hollywood Awards">Young Hollywood Award for Breakthrough Performance</a>. Her leading role of <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Flick" title="Tracy Flick">Tracy Flick</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Election_(1999_film)" title="Election (1999 film)">Election</a></i> was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Comedy_or_Musical" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Motion Picture Comedy or Musical">Golden Globe Award</a>.</p>
<p>Witherspoon's breakthrough role was playing <a href="/wiki/Elle_Woods" title="Elle Woods">Elle Woods</a> in the 2001 film <i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blonde" title="Legally Blonde">Legally Blonde</a></i>, for which she received international recognition and her second Golden Globe nomination. The following year, she starred in the romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Sweet_Home_Alabama_(film)" title="Sweet Home Alabama (film)">Sweet Home Alabama</a></i> (2002), which emerged as her biggest live-action commercial success. In 2005, Witherspoon received worldwide attention for her portrayal of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/June_Carter" title="June Carter">June Carter</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Walk_the_Line" title="Walk the Line">Walk the Line</a></i>, which earned her the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Motion_Picture_%E2%80%93_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress in a Motion Picture – Drama">Golden Globe Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Female_Actor_in_a_Leading_Role" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Leading Role">Screen Actors Guild Award</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Critics%27_Choice_Movie_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Critics' Choice Movie Award for Best Actress">Critics Choice Award</a> for Best Actress. Her other films include <i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blonde_2:_Red,_White_%26_Blonde" title="Legally Blonde 2: Red, White &amp; Blonde">Legally Blonde 2: Red, White &amp; Blonde</a></i> (2003); <i><a href="/wiki/Monsters_vs._Aliens" title="Monsters vs. Aliens">Monsters vs. Aliens</a></i> (2009); <i><a href="/wiki/Water_for_Elephants_(film)" title="Water for Elephants (film)">Water for Elephants</a></i> (2011) and <i><a href="/wiki/Sing_(2016_film)" title="Sing (2016 film)">Sing</a></i> (2016). In 2014, Witherspoon produced the thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Gone_Girl_(film)" title="Gone Girl (film)">Gone Girl</a></i> and received critical acclaim for portraying <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_Strayed" title="Cheryl Strayed">Cheryl Strayed</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Wild_(2014_film)" title="Wild (2014 film)">Wild</a></i>, for which she earned her second Academy Award nomination for Best Actress.</p>
<p>Witherspoon owns a production company, Pacific Standard, and she is actively involved in children's and women's advocacy organizations. She serves on the board of the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Defense_Fund" title="Children's Defense Fund">Children's Defense Fund</a> (CDF) and was named Global Ambassador of <a href="/wiki/Avon_Products" title="Avon Products">Avon Products</a> in 2007, serving as honorary chair of the charitable Avon Foundation. Witherspoon received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> on December 1, 2010.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Witherspoon was born on March 22, 1976<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Ochsner_Baptist_Medical_Center" title="Ochsner Baptist Medical Center">Southern Baptist Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>, Louisiana, while her father, Dr. John Draper Witherspoon, was a student at <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">Tulane University</a> medical school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tulane_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-tulane-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dork_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-dork-4">[4]</a></sup> Her father was born in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> and served as a lieutenant colonel in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Reserve" title="United States Army Reserve">United States Army Reserve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movieyahoo_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-movieyahoo-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-That.27s_Reese_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-That.27s_Reese-6">[6]</a></sup> He was in private practice as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otolaryngology" title="Otolaryngology">otolaryngologist</a> until 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Her mother, Mary Elizabeth "Betty" (née Reese), is from <a href="/wiki/Harriman,_Tennessee" title="Harriman, Tennessee">Harriman, Tennessee</a>, and earned a BS and master's degrees in Nursing, and a doctor of education;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> she worked as a professor of nursing (child care and mental health) at <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_University" title="Vanderbilt University">Vanderbilt University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-That.27s_Reese_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-That.27s_Reese-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali1_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-tiscali1-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1988, her mother began nursing babies back to health in the <a href="/wiki/Neonatal_intensive_care_unit" title="Neonatal intensive care unit">neonatal intensive care unit</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_University_Hospital" title="Vanderbilt University Hospital">Vanderbilt University Hospital</a> until she retired. Witherspoon has claimed descent from Scottish-born <a href="/wiki/John_Witherspoon" title="John Witherspoon">John Witherspoon</a>, who signed the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsindependent_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsindependent-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> however, this claim has not been verified by the Society of the Descendants of the Signers of the Declaration of Independence genealogists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Her parents are still legally married, although they separated in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because Witherspoon's father worked for the U.S. military in <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a>, Germany, she lived there for four years as a child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali1_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-tiscali1-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livingscot_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-livingscot-15">[15]</a></sup> After returning to the U.S., she spent her childhood in <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a> in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Belle_Meade,_Tennessee" title="Belle Meade, Tennessee">Belle Meade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali1_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-tiscali1-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livingscot_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-livingscot-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> She was raised as an Episcopalian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reader.27s_digest_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-reader.27s_digest-17">[17]</a></sup> Her older brother, John Jr. is a real estate agent. She received high grades in school,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-tiscali2-18">[18]</a></sup> loved reading, and considered herself "a big dork who read loads of books."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dork_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-dork-4">[4]</a></sup> On mentioning her love for books, she said, "I get crazy in a bookstore. It makes my heart beat hard because I want to buy everything."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reader.27s_digest_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-reader.27s_digest-17">[17]</a></sup> Witherspoon attended middle school at Harding Academy and graduated from the all-girls' <a href="/wiki/Harpeth_Hall_School" title="Harpeth Hall School">Harpeth Hall School</a> in Nashville, during which time she was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheerleader" title="Cheerleader">cheerleader</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-page1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-page1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talent_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-talent-20">[20]</a></sup> She attended <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> as an English literature major.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commitment_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-commitment-21">[21]</a></sup> After completing one year of studies, she left Stanford to pursue an acting career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talent_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-talent-20">[20]</a></sup> Witherspoon is proud of the "definitive <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="Culture of the Southern United States">Southern</a> upbringing" which she received. She said that it gave her "a sense of family and tradition" and taught her about "being conscientious about people's feelings, being polite, being responsible and never taking for granted what you have in your life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talent_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-talent-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sweethome_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-sweethome-22">[22]</a></sup> Witherspoon is described as a "multi-achiever" and was given the nickname "Little Type A" by her parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ambition_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-ambition-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fashion_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-fashion-24">[24]</a></sup> On discussing her early achievements, she told <i><a href="/wiki/Interview_(magazine)" title="Interview (magazine)">Interview</a></i> magazine, "I just don't see any of it as that remarkable. Maybe that's the attitude I choose to have to keep me sane and keep my feet on the ground. I grew up in an environment where women accomplished a lot. And if they weren't able to, it was because they were limited by society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-That.27s_Reese_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-That.27s_Reese-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the age of seven, Witherspoon was selected as a model for a florist's television advertisements, which motivated her to take acting lessons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali2_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-tiscali2-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> At age eleven, she took first place in the Ten-State Talent Fair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali2_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-tiscali2-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_career">Acting career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Acting career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1991.E2.80.9398">1991–98</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1991–98">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1991, Witherspoon attended an open casting call for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_in_the_Moon" title="The Man in the Moon">The Man in the Moon</a></i>, intending to audition as a bit player;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talent_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-talent-20">[20]</a></sup> she was instead cast for the lead role of Dani Trant, a 14-year-old country girl who falls in love for the first time with her 17-year-old neighbor. Her performance was regarded as "memorably touching" by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Variety_magazine" title="Variety magazine">Variety</a></i> magazine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fear_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-fear-26">[26]</a></sup> and critic <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> commented, "Her first kiss is one of the most perfect little scenes I've ever seen in a movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali2_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-tiscali2-18">[18]</a></sup> For this role, Witherspoon was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Young_Artist_Award" title="Young Artist Award">Young Artist Award</a> Best Young Actress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-award_13th_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-award_13th-27">[27]</a></sup> Later that year, she made her television debut role in <i><a href="/wiki/Wildflower_(1991_film)" title="Wildflower (1991 film)">Wildflower</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Arquette" title="Patricia Arquette">Patricia Arquette</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movieyahoo_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-movieyahoo-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsindependent_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-newsindependent-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1992, Witherspoon appeared in the TV movie <i>Desperate Choices: To Save My Child</i>, portraying a critically ill young girl.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movieyahoo_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-movieyahoo-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993, she played a young wife in the <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Return_to_Lonesome_Dove" title="Return to Lonesome Dove">Return to Lonesome Dove</a></i>, Nonnie Parker in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">Disney</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Far_Off_Place" title="A Far Off Place">A Far Off Place</a></i> and had a minor role in <i><a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Bear" title="Jack the Bear">Jack the Bear</a></i>, which garnered her the Young Artist Award for Best Youth Actress Co-star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movieyahoo_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-movieyahoo-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-award_15th_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-award_15th-28">[28]</a></sup> The next year, Witherspoon had another leading role as Wendy Pfister in the 1994 film <i><a href="/wiki/S.F.W." title="S.F.W.">S.F.W.</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Jefery_Levy" title="Jefery Levy">Jefery Levy</a>. In 1996, Witherspoon starred in two major films, the thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Fear_(1996_film)" title="Fear (1996 film)">Fear</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a> (whom she dated),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv-29">[29]</a></sup> as Nicole Walker, a teenage girl who starts dating a man with obsessive tendencies, and the black-comedy thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Freeway_(1996_film)" title="Freeway (1996 film)">Freeway</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Kiefer_Sutherland" title="Kiefer Sutherland">Kiefer Sutherland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brooke_Shields" title="Brooke Shields">Brooke Shields</a>, where she had the lead role. Her character, Vanessa Lutz, is a poor girl living in Los Angeles, who encounters a <a href="/wiki/Serial_killer" title="Serial killer">serial killer</a> on the way to her grandmother's home in <a href="/wiki/Stockton,_California" title="Stockton, California">Stockton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talent_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-talent-20">[20]</a></sup> The film received positive reviews from the press. Among them was the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i>, with <a href="/wiki/Mick_LaSalle" title="Mick LaSalle">Mick LaSalle</a> commenting, "Witherspoon, who does a Texas accent, is dazzling, utterly believable in one extreme situation after the other."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Witherspoon's performance won her the Best Actress Award at the <a href="/wiki/Festival_du_Film_Policier_de_Cognac" title="Festival du Film Policier de Cognac">Cognac Police Film Festival</a> and firmly established her as a rising star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talent_20-5"><a href="#cite_note-talent-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The making of the film also gave Witherspoon significant acting experience; as she said, "Once I overcame the hurdle of that movie – which scared me to death – I felt like I could try anything."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commitment_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-commitment-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998, Witherspoon had major roles in three movies: <i><a href="/wiki/Overnight_Delivery" title="Overnight Delivery">Overnight Delivery</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pleasantville_(film)" title="Pleasantville (film)">Pleasantville</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Twilight_(1998_film)" title="Twilight (1998 film)">Twilight</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsindependent_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-newsindependent-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spoonful_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-spoonful-32">[32]</a></sup> In <i>Pleasantville</i>, she starred with <a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">Tobey Maguire</a> in a tale about 1990s teenage siblings who are magically transported into the setting of a 1950s television series. She portrayed the sister, Jennifer, who is mainly concerned about appearances, relationships and popularity. Her performance received good reviews and garnered her the Young Hollywood Award for Best Female Breakthrough Performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Director <a href="/wiki/Gary_Ross" title="Gary Ross">Gary Ross</a> said he firmly believed Witherspoon would be an outstanding movie star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commitment_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-commitment-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1999.E2.80.932000">1999–2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1999–2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1999, Witherspoon starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Nivola" title="Alessandro Nivola">Alessandro Nivola</a> in the drama thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Best_Laid_Plans_(1999_film)" title="Best Laid Plans (1999 film)">Best Laid Plans</a></i>; she played Lissa, a woman who schemes with her lover Nick to escape a small dead-end town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movieyahoo_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-movieyahoo-5">[5]</a></sup> Also that year co-starred with <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Michelle_Gellar" title="Sarah Michelle Gellar">Sarah Michelle Gellar</a> and Ryan Phillippe in the drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Cruel_Intentions" title="Cruel Intentions">Cruel Intentions</a></i>, a modern take on the 18th-century French novel <i><a href="/wiki/Les_Liaisons_dangereuses" title="Les Liaisons dangereuses">Les Liaisons Dangereuses</a></i>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="The San Francisco Chronicle">The San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> praised her performance as Annette Hargrove: "Witherspoon is especially good in the least flashy role, and even when called upon to make a series of cute devilish faces, she pulls it off."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> She also appeared in a music video by <a href="/wiki/Marcy_Playground" title="Marcy Playground">Marcy Playground</a> for the film's soundtrack and starred with <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Broderick" title="Matthew Broderick">Matthew Broderick</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Election_(1999_film)" title="Election (1999 film)">Election</a></i> which is based on <a href="/wiki/Tom_Perrotta" title="Tom Perrotta">Tom Perrotta</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Election_(1998_novel)" title="Election (1998 novel)">novel</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movieyahoo_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-movieyahoo-5">[5]</a></sup> For her portrayal of <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Flick" title="Tracy Flick">Tracy Flick</a>, she received vast critical acclaim and won the Best Actress Award from the <a href="/wiki/National_Society_of_Film_Critics" title="National Society of Film Critics">National Society of Film Critics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Online_Film_Critics_Society" title="Online Film Critics Society">Online Film Critics Society</a>, a first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> nomination and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_Spirit_Award" title="Independent Spirit Award">Independent Spirit Award</a> nomination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Witherspoon also received a rank on the list of <i>100 Greatest Film Performances of All Time</i> by <i><a href="/wiki/Premiere_(magazine)" title="Premiere (magazine)">Premiere</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Director <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Payne" title="Alexander Payne">Alexander Payne</a> said of her, "She's got that quality that men find attractive, while women would like to be her friend. But that's just the foundation. Nobody else is as funny or brings such charm to things. She can do anything."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sweethome_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-sweethome-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In spite of her success with <i>Election</i>, Witherspoon noted in an interview that she struggled to find work after completing the film, due to <a href="/wiki/Typecasting_(acting)" title="Typecasting (acting)">typecasting</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Analyzing the reasons behind her difficulty to find work, Witherspoon commented, "I think because the character I played was so extreme and sort of shrewish—people thought that was who I was, rather than me going in and creating a part. I would audition for things and I'd always be the second choice—studios never wanted to hire me and I wasn't losing the parts to big box office actresses but to ones who I guess people felt differently about."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-That.27s_Reese_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-That.27s_Reese-6">[6]</a></sup> In 2000, Witherspoon played a supporting role in <i><a href="/wiki/American_Psycho_(film)" title="American Psycho (film)">American Psycho</a></i> and made a cameo appearance in <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Nicky" title="Little Nicky">Little Nicky</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spoonful_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-spoonful-32">[32]</a></sup> She also guest starred in season six of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friends_(TV_series)" title="Friends (TV series)">Friends</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Green" title="Rachel Green">Rachel Green</a>'s sister Jill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The next year, Witherspoon voiced Serena in the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Trumpet_of_the_Swan_(film)" title="The Trumpet of the Swan (film)">The Trumpet of the Swan</a></i>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Crest_Animation_Productions" title="Crest Animation Productions">Crest Animation Productions</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2001.E2.80.9304">2001–04</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2001–04">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2001 film <i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blonde" title="Legally Blonde">Legally Blonde</a></i> marked a turning point in Witherspoon's career; she starred as Elle Woods, a fashion-merchandising major who decides to become a law student in order to follow her ex-boyfriend to <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Law_School" title="Harvard Law School">Harvard Law School</a>. Witherspoon said about the role, "When I read <i>Legally Blonde</i>, I was like, 'She's from Beverly Hills, she's rich, she's in a sorority. She has a great boyfriend. Oh yeah, she gets dumped. Who cares? I still hate her.' So we had to make sure she was the kind of person you just can't hate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sweethome_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-sweethome-22">[22]</a></sup> <i>Legally Blonde</i> was a box-office hit, grossing US$96 million domestically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-40">[40]</a></sup> Witherspoon's performance earned her praise from critics, as the press began referring to her as "the new <a href="/wiki/Meg_Ryan" title="Meg Ryan">Meg Ryan</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> commented, "Witherspoon effortlessly animated this material with sunshine and quick wit",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon.com</a> noted that "she [Witherspoon] delineates Elle's character beautifully".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the <i><a href="/wiki/Seattle_Post-Intelligencer" title="Seattle Post-Intelligencer">Seattle Post-Intelligencer</a></i> concluded, "Witherspoon is a talented comedian who can perk up a scene just by marching in full of pep and drive and she powers this modest little comedy almost single-handedly."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> For her work, Witherspoon garnered her second <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe</a> Best Actress nomination and an <a href="/wiki/2002_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2002 MTV Movie Awards">MTV Movie Award</a> for Best Comedic Performance.</p>
<p>In 2002, after the success of <i>Legally Blonde</i>, Witherspoon starred in several roles, such as Greta Wolfcastle in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Bart_Wants_What_It_Wants" title="The Bart Wants What It Wants">The Bart Wants What It Wants</a>", and as Cecily in the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Importance_of_Being_Earnest_(2002_film)" title="The Importance of Being Earnest (2002 film)">The Importance of Being Earnest</a></i>, a film adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wilde" title="Oscar Wilde">Oscar Wilde</a>'s play in which she received a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Award" title="Teen Choice Award">Teen Choice Award</a> nomination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Later that year, she starred with <a href="/wiki/Josh_Lucas" title="Josh Lucas">Josh Lucas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Dempsey" title="Patrick Dempsey">Patrick Dempsey</a> in <a href="/wiki/Andy_Tennant" title="Andy Tennant">Andy Tennant</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Sweet_Home_Alabama_(film)" title="Sweet Home Alabama (film)">Sweet Home Alabama</a></i>, where she played Melanie Carmichael, a young fashion designer who intends to marry a New York politician but must return to <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> to divorce her childhood sweetheart, from whom she has been separated for seven years. Witherspoon regarded this as a "personal role", in that it reminded her of experiences she had when she moved from her hometown Nashville to Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The movie became Witherspoon's biggest box office hit to date, earning over $35 million in the opening weekend and grossing over $127 million in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Despite the commercial success, critics gave <i>Sweet Home Alabama</i> negative reviews. It was called "a romantic comedy so rote, dull and predictable" by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Miami_Herald" title="The Miami Herald">The Miami Herald</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> and the press widely agreed that Witherspoon was the only reason the movie attracted such a large audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> When describing Witherspoon's role in the movie, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor" title="The Christian Science Monitor">The Christian Science Monitor</a></i> concluded, "She is not the movie's main attraction, she is its only attraction."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, Witherspoon followed up the success of <i>Legally Blonde</i> by starring in the sequel <i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blonde_2:_Red,_White_%26_Blonde" title="Legally Blonde 2: Red, White &amp; Blonde">Legally Blonde 2: Red, White &amp; Blonde</a></i>. Elle Woods has become a Harvard-educated lawyer who is determined to protect animals from cosmetics-industry science tests. The sequel was not as financially successful as the first film and it generated mostly negative reviews. <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> considered the movie "plodding, unfunny and almost cringe-worthy", but also noted that "Reese Witherspoon still does a fine job portraying the fair-haired lovable brainiac, but her top-notch comic timing is wasted on the humorless dialogue."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Salon.com concluded that the sequel "calcifies everything that was enjoyable about the first movie".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Despite being panned by critics, the sequel took in over $39 million in its first five days in the U.S. box office charts and eventually grossed $90 million in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Witherspoon received a $15 million paycheck for the role—a starting point to make her consistently one of Hollywood's highest-paid actresses from 2002 until 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sweethome_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-sweethome-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In 2004, Witherspoon starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(2004_film)" title="Vanity Fair (2004 film)">Vanity Fair</a></i>, adapted from the 19th-century classic novel <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(novel)" title="Vanity Fair (novel)">Vanity Fair</a></i> and directed by <a href="/wiki/Mira_Nair" title="Mira Nair">Mira Nair</a>. Her character, Becky Sharp, is a poor woman with a ruthless determination to find fortune and establish herself a position in society. Witherspoon was carefully costumed to conceal that during the filming she was pregnant with her second child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> This pregnancy was not a hindrance to her work as Witherspoon believed the gestation had in fact helped her portrayal of Sharp's character: "I love the luminosity that pregnancy brings, I love the fleshiness, I love the ample bosom—it gave me much more to play with", she said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraphindia_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphindia-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The film and Witherspoon's portrayal of Sharp received positive reviews, as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> wrote, "Nair's cast is splendid. Witherspoon does justice to the juicy role by giving the part more buoyancy than naughtiness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> At the same time, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Charlotte_Observer" title="The Charlotte Observer">The Charlotte Observer</a></i> called her work "an excellent performance that's soft around the edges" and the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> concluded that Becky is "a role Reese Witherspoon was born to play".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.9306:_Walk_the_Line_and_critical_achievements">2005–06: <i>Walk the Line</i> and critical achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2005–06: Walk the Line and critical achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In late 2004, Witherspoon began working alongside <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ruffalo" title="Mark Ruffalo">Mark Ruffalo</a> on the romantic comedy <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Just_Like_Heaven_(film)" title="Just Like Heaven (film)">Just Like Heaven</a></i>. Her character, Elizabeth Masterson, is an ambitious young doctor who gets into a car accident on her way to a blind date and is left in a coma; her spirit returns to her old apartment where she later finds true love.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="774" data-file-width="985" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg/220px-Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg/330px-Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg/440px-Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon2_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Witherspoon at the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a> premiere of <i>Walk the Line</i> in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Earlier that year Witherspoon was chosen to portray <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">June Carter Cash</a>, the second wife of country music singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a> (<a href="/wiki/Joaquin_Phoenix" title="Joaquin Phoenix">Joaquin Phoenix</a>), in <i><a href="/wiki/Walk_the_Line" title="Walk the Line">Walk the Line</a></i>. She never had the chance to meet Carter Cash, as Witherspoon was filming <i>Vanity Fair</i> at the time Carter Cash died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-That.27s_Reese_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-That.27s_Reese-6">[6]</a></sup> Witherspoon performed her own vocals in the film and her songs had to be performed in front of a live audience, she was so worried about needing to perform live that she asked her lawyer to terminate the film contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faces_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-faces-66">[66]</a></sup> "That was the most challenging part of the role," she later recalled in an interview, "I'd never sung professionally."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Subsequently, she had to spend six months learning how to sing for the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faces_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-faces-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Witherspoon's portrayal of Carter Cash was well received by critics, and Roger Ebert wrote that her performance added "boundless energy" to the movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> She won several awards for her performance, including the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Comedy_or_Musical" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Motion Picture Comedy or Musical">Golden Globe Award</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award for Best Actress</a> in a Lead Role. Besides critical success in the movie industry, Witherspoon and Phoenix received a nomination for "collaborative video of the year" from the <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-academy-award-bbc_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-academy-award-bbc-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Witherspoon expressed her passion for the movie: "I really like in this film that it is realistic and portrays sort of a real marriage, a real relationship where there are forbidden thoughts and fallibility. And it is about compassion in the long haul, not just the short easy solutions to problems."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about.interview_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-about.interview-72">[72]</a></sup> She also stated that she believed Carter Cash was a woman ahead of her time: "I think the really remarkable thing about her character is that she did all of these things that we sort of see as normal things in the 1950s when it wasn't really acceptable for a woman to be married and divorced twice and have two different children by two different husbands and travel around in a car full of very famous musicians all by herself. She didn't try to comply to social convention, so I think that makes her a very modern woman."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about.interview_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-about.interview-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Witherspoon's first post-Oscar role came in the modern-day fairy tale <i><a href="/wiki/Penelope_(2006_film)" title="Penelope (2006 film)">Penelope</a></i>, as Annie, the best friend of Penelope (<a href="/wiki/Christina_Ricci" title="Christina Ricci">Christina Ricci</a>), a girl who has a curse in her family. The film was produced by her company <a href="/wiki/Type_A_Films" title="Type A Films">Type A Films</a>, with filming commencing in March 2006, immediately following Witherspoon's Oscar win for <i>Walk the Line</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Although the movie premiered at the <a href="/wiki/2006_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2006 Toronto International Film Festival">2006 Toronto International Film Festival</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faces_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-faces-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> the final release date of <i>Penelope</i> was delayed twice before an eventual February 2008 release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.E2.80.9312:_Creative_struggles_and_.22love_triangle_period.22">2007–12: Creative struggles and "love triangle period"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title='Edit section: 2007–12: Creative struggles and "love triangle period"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following her critical success with <i>Walk the Line</i>, Witherspoon admits to spending several years "kind of floundering career-wise". Reflecting on this period of time in a December 2014 interview, Witherspoon attributed it to her separation from her first husband in October 2006 and their subsequent divorce, stating that she spent "a few years just trying to feel better. You know, you can't really be very creative when you feel like your brain is scrambled eggs." She claims that she "wasn't making things I was passionate about. I was just kind of working, you know. And it was really clear that audiences weren't responding to anything I was putting out there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>This period of Witherspoon's career began with the filming of the abduction thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Rendition_(film)" title="Rendition (film)">Rendition</a></i> in November 2006. In the film, she plays Isabella El-Ibrahim, the pregnant wife of a bombing suspect. The film was released in October 2007 and marked Witherspoon's first appearance in theaters since the 2005 release of <i>Walk the Line</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The movie received mostly negative reviews and was generally considered a disappointment at the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Witherspoon's performance was also criticized: "Reese Witherspoon is surprisingly lifeless", <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> wrote, "She customarily injects energy and spirit into her parts, but here, her performance feels tamped down."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_2011,_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1868" data-file-width="1783" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Reese_Witherspoon_2011%2C_2.jpg/220px-Reese_Witherspoon_2011%2C_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Reese_Witherspoon_2011%2C_2.jpg/330px-Reese_Witherspoon_2011%2C_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Reese_Witherspoon_2011%2C_2.jpg/440px-Reese_Witherspoon_2011%2C_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_2011,_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Witherspoon at the <i>Water for Elephants</i> premiere in May 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In December 2007, Witherspoon began working with <a href="/wiki/Vince_Vaughn" title="Vince Vaughn">Vince Vaughn</a>, filming the holiday comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Four_Christmases" title="Four Christmases">Four Christmases</a></i>, a story about a couple who must spend their Christmas Day trying to visit all four of their divorced parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The film was released in November 2008. Despite receiving only average reviews by critics, the movie became a box-office success, earning more than 120 million US dollars domestically and 157 million US dollars worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> In 2009, Witherspoon voiced Susan Murphy, the main character in <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks</a>' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer-animated" title="Computer-animated">computer-animated</a> 3-D feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Monsters_vs._Aliens" title="Monsters vs. Aliens">Monsters vs. Aliens</a></i>, released in March 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and she also co-produced the <i>Legally Blonde</i> spin-off <i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blondes" title="Legally Blondes">Legally Blondes</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Camilla_and_Rebecca_Rosso" title="Camilla and Rebecca Rosso">Milly and Becky Rosso</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, Witherspoon did not appear in a live-action film for two years after the 2008 release of <i>Four Christmases</i>. She told <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> that the "break" was unplanned, stating that, "I just didn't read anything I liked... There are a lot of really, really, really big movies about robots and things—and there's not a part for a 34-year-old woman in a robot movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Witherspoon returned with three films released in 2010, 2011 and 2012, all centered on her as a woman caught in a love triangle between two men. In a 2012 interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>, Witherspoon jokingly referred to this trio of films as her "love triangle period".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first film was <a href="/wiki/James_L._Brooks" title="James L. Brooks">James L. Brooks</a>'s romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Know" title="How Do You Know">How Do You Know</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> which starred Witherspoon as a former national softball player who struggles to choose between a baseball star boyfriend (<a href="/wiki/Owen_Wilson" title="Owen Wilson">Owen Wilson</a>) and a business executive being investigated for <a href="/wiki/White-collar_crime" title="White-collar crime">white-collar crime</a> (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Rudd" title="Paul Rudd">Paul Rudd</a>). The movie was filmed in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> during the summer and fall of 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> and released on December 17, 2010. The movie was both a critical and box office failure. Despite an over-$100 million budget, the film earned only $7.6 million in its opening weekend, leading the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> to call it "one of the year's biggest flops".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The movie earned mainly negative reviews from critics, scoring 35% on <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> with 111 reviews as of late December 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Witherspoon's second love-triangle movie was the film adaptation of the 1930s circus drama <i><a href="/wiki/Water_for_Elephants_(film)" title="Water for Elephants (film)">Water for Elephants</a></i>. She began circus training in March 2010 for her role as Marlena, a glamorous performer stuck in a marriage to a volatile husband (<a href="/wiki/Christoph_Waltz" title="Christoph Waltz">Christoph Waltz</a>) but intrigued by the circus's new veterinarian (<a href="/wiki/Robert_Pattinson" title="Robert Pattinson">Robert Pattinson</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The movie was filmed between late May and early August 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> in various locations in <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. It was released on April 22, 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and received mixed critical reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2010, Witherspoon began <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">principal photography</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> for the third love-triangle film, <i><a href="/wiki/This_Means_War_(film)" title="This Means War (film)">This Means War</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> spy comedy directed by <a href="/wiki/McG" title="McG">McG</a> in which Witherspoon's character is at the center of a battle between best friends (played by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Pine" title="Chris Pine">Chris Pine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a>) who are both in love with her. The film had a "sneak-peek" release on <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine's Day">Valentine's Day</a>, before fully opening on February 17, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The film was panned by critics (with a 25% <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> rating),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and fared poorly at the box office, taking fifth place on its opening weekend with sales of $17.6 million. The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> remarked that this "extended the box office cold streak for the Oscar-winning Ms. Witherspoon."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013.E2.80.93present:_Renewed_critical_success_.E2.80.93_Wild_and_beyond">2013–present: Renewed critical success – <i>Wild</i> and beyond</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2013–present: Renewed critical success – Wild and beyond">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="629" data-file-width="455" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg/170px-Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg/255px-Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg/340px-Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_Cannes_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Witherspoon at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2012 Cannes Film Festival">2012 Cannes Film Festival</a> premiere of <i>Mud</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Witherspoon's subsequent films signaled a departure from the love-triangle theme. In September 2011, a year after beginning work on <i>This Means War</i>, she filmed a small role in <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Nichols" title="Jeff Nichols">Jeff Nichols</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coming-of-age_film" title="Coming-of-age film">coming-of-age</a> drama <i><a href="/wiki/Mud_(2012_film)" title="Mud (2012 film)">Mud</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, playing Juniper, the former girlfriend of a fugitive (<a href="/wiki/Matthew_McConaughey" title="Matthew McConaughey">Matthew McConaughey</a>), who enlists two local boys to help him evade capture and rekindle his romance with her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <i>Mud</i> premiered in May 2012 in competition for the <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Or</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2012 Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>, but did not win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Following its American debut at the <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> on January 19, 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> the film had a <a href="/wiki/Limited_release" title="Limited release">limited release</a> in select North American theaters on April 26, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Witherspoon next starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Knot_(film)" title="Devil's Knot (film)">Devil's Knot</a></i>, which is based on <a href="/wiki/Atom_Egoyan" title="Atom Egoyan">Atom Egoyan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/True_crime" title="True crime">true crime</a> book of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Knot" title="Devil's Knot">same name</a> and examines the controversial case of the <a href="/wiki/West_Memphis_Three" title="West Memphis Three">West Memphis Three</a>. Like <i>Mud</i>, the film is set in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>. Witherspoon played Pam Hobbs, the mother of one of three young murder victims. In an interview subsequent to her casting in the film, Egoyan noted that although the role requires "an emotionally loaded journey", he "met with Reese, and... talked at length about the project, and she's eager to take on the challenge".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The movie was shot in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> in June and July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devil_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-devil-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knot_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-knot-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devilsknot2_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-devilsknot2-117">[117]</a></sup> Witherspoon was pregnant with her third child during filming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devilsknot3_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-devilsknot3-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devilsknot4_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-devilsknot4-119">[119]</a></sup> The film's world premiere was held on September 8, 2013 at the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> It was then released in selected American theaters on May 9, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2013, Witherspoon began production in Atlanta on Canadian director <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Falardeau" title="Philippe Falardeau">Philippe Falardeau</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Lie" title="The Good Lie">The Good Lie</a></i>. It is based on real-life events, about a brash American woman assigned to help four young <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_Sudan" title="Refugees of Sudan">Sudanese refugees</a> (known as <a href="/wiki/Lost_Boys_of_Sudan" title="Lost Boys of Sudan">Lost Boys of Sudan</a>) who win a lottery for relocation to the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thegoodlie1_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-thegoodlie1-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thegoodlie2_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-thegoodlie2-124">[124]</a></sup> It was released on October 3, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Witherspoon shot a small role in <i><a href="/wiki/Inherent_Vice_(film)" title="Inherent Vice (film)">Inherent Vice</a></i> (2014), an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pynchon" title="Thomas Pynchon">Thomas Pynchon</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Inherent_Vice" title="Inherent Vice">novel</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a> in summer 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Through her company Pacific Standard, Witherspoon served as a producer in the <a href="/wiki/Gone_Girl_(film)" title="Gone Girl (film)">film adaptation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gillian_Flynn" title="Gillian Flynn">Gillian Flynn</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Gone_Girl_(novel)" title="Gone Girl (novel)">Gone Girl</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> though she did not star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Indeed, Witherspoon and her producing partner "had little to do with the production of <i>Gone Girl</i>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> leaving it to director <a href="/wiki/David_Fincher" title="David Fincher">David Fincher</a> while focusing their efforts on another adaptation produced via Pacific Standard, that of <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_Strayed" title="Cheryl Strayed">Cheryl Strayed</a>'s memoir <i><a href="/wiki/Wild:_From_Lost_to_Found_on_the_Pacific_Crest_Trail" title="Wild: From Lost to Found on the Pacific Crest Trail">Wild</a></i>, which began production in fall 2013 on the same day as <i>Gone Girl</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Witherspoon starred in the project, portraying Strayed herself on her 1,000-mile (1,600 km) hike along the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Crest_Trail" title="Pacific Crest Trail">Pacific Crest Trail</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Wild_(2014_film)" title="Wild (2014 film)">Wild</a></i> was released in December 2014 to critical acclaim;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Michael Phillips of <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> wrote in his review, "Witherspoon does the least acting of her career, and it works. Calmly yet restlessly, she brings to life Strayed's longings, her states of grief and desire and her wary optimism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> <i>Wild</i> was promoted as Witherspoon's primary "comeback" vehicle following her previous career slump,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and she earned her second Academy Award nomination for the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2014, Witherspoon began production in Louisiana on <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_Pursuit_(2015_film)" title="Hot Pursuit (2015 film)">Hot Pursuit</a></i>, a comedy in which she plays a police officer trying to protect a drug lord's widow (<a href="/wiki/Sof%C3%ADa_Vergara" title="Sofía Vergara">Sofía Vergara</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The movie was released on May 8, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2016, she had a voice role in the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Sing_(2016_film)" title="Sing (2016 film)">Sing</a></i>, as well as serving as a major performer on the film's soundtrack. The movie became Witherspoon's biggest hit, being the first to make over $200 million domestically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="1219" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg/170px-Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg/255px-Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg/340px-Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Witherspoon at the <a href="/wiki/69th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="69th Golden Globe Awards">69th Annual Golden Globe Awards</a> in January 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Witherspoon owned a production company called Type A Films, which the media believed was a moniker honoring her childhood nickname "Little Miss Type A."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ambition_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-ambition-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> However, when asked about the company by <i><a href="/wiki/Interview_(magazine)" title="Interview (magazine)">Interview</a></i> magazine, she clarified the name's origin: "... people think I named it after myself... It was actually an <a href="/wiki/In-joke" title="In-joke">in-joke</a> with my family because at [age] 7 I understood complicated medical terms, such as the difference between <a href="/wiki/Type_A_and_Type_B_personality_theory" title="Type A and Type B personality theory">type A and type B personalities</a>. But I just wished I'd named the company Dogfood Films or Fork or something. You carry that baggage all your life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-That.27s_Reese_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-That.27s_Reese-6">[6]</a></sup> In March 2012, Witherspoon merged Type A Films with producer <a href="/wiki/Bruna_Papandrea" title="Bruna Papandrea">Bruna Papandrea</a>'s Make Movies banner to create a new production company entitled Pacific Standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> In 2016, Witherspoon and Papandrea split up, with Witherspoon gaining full control over the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Witherspoon recorded a cover of the classic <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Sinatra" title="Nancy Sinatra">Nancy Sinatra</a> duet, "<a href="/wiki/Somethin%27_Stupid" title="Somethin' Stupid">Somethin' Stupid</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bubl%C3%A9" title="Michael Bublé">Michael Bublé</a> for his 2013 album, <i><a href="/wiki/To_Be_Loved" title="To Be Loved">To Be Loved</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2015, Witherspoon launched <a href="/wiki/Draper_James" title="Draper James">Draper James</a>, a retail brand with a focus on fashion, accessories and home décor inspired by the American South. The brand is named after Witherspoon's grandparents, Dorothea Draper and William James Witherspoon, who are said to be her greatest influences. Some of the products are being manufactured and designed in-house, and the brand launched direct to consumers online before opening its first brick and mortar store in fall 2015 in Witherspoon's hometown of <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2016, Witherspoon and <a href="/wiki/Otter_Media" title="Otter Media">Otter Media</a> formed Hello Sunshine, a joint venture focused on telling female-driven stories on film, TV and digital platforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Witherspoon is actively involved in children's and women's advocacy organizations. She is a longtime supporter of <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a>, an organization that helps provide children around the world with education, health care and emergency aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chldrn_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-chldrn-148">[148]</a></sup> She also serves on the board of the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Defense_Fund" title="Children's Defense Fund">Children's Defense Fund</a>, a child advocacy and research group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chldrn_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-chldrn-148">[148]</a></sup> In 2006, she was among a group of actresses who went to New Orleans, Louisiana in a CDF project to publicize the needs of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> victims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> During this trip, she helped open the city's first Freedom School, as she met and talked with the children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trip_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-trip-150">[150]</a></sup> Witherspoon later called this an experience that she would never forget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trip_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-trip-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, Witherspoon made her first move into the world of endorsements, as she signed a multi-year agreement to serve as the first Global Ambassador of cosmetic company <a href="/wiki/Avon_Products" title="Avon Products">Avon Products</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chldrn_148-2"><a href="#cite_note-chldrn-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avon_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-avon-151">[151]</a></sup> She acts as a spokeswoman for Avon's cosmetic products and serves as the honorary chair of the <i>Avon Foundation</i>, a charitable organization that supports women and focuses on breast cancer research and the prevention of domestic violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avon_products_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-avon_products-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Witherspoon is also committed to participating in cosmetics product development and appearing in commercial advertisements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avon_products_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-avon_products-152">[152]</a></sup> Explaining her motives for joining the foundation, she said, "As a woman and a mother I care deeply about the well being of other women and children throughout the world and through the years, I have always looked for opportunities to make a difference."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avon_products_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-avon_products-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_media">In the media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reese_Witherspoon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: In the media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1082" data-file-width="668" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg/170px-Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg/255px-Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg/340px-Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reese_Witherspoon_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Witherspoon being interviewed at the premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Walk_the_Line" title="Walk the Line">Walk the Line</a></i> in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Witherspoon hosted <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> on September 29, 2001, the first episode to air after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> In 2005, she was ranked No. 5 in <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">Teen People</a></i> magazine's list of most powerful young Hollywood actors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> In 2006, Witherspoon was listed among the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">Time 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Her featured article was written by <a href="/wiki/Luke_Wilson" title="Luke Wilson">Luke Wilson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> In the same year, she was selected as one of the "<a href="/wiki/FHM%27s_100_Sexiest_Women_(UK)" title="FHM's 100 Sexiest Women (UK)">100 Sexiest Women In The World</a>" by the readers of <i><a href="/wiki/FHM" title="FHM">FHM</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> Witherspoon has been featured four times in the annual "100 Most Beautiful" issues of <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Witherspoon has appeared on the annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celebrity_100" title="Celebrity 100">Celebrity 100</a> list by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine in 2006 and 2007, at No. 75 and No. 80, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> also put her on the top ten Trustworthy Celebrities list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> She was listed among <i>CEOWorld Magazine'</i>s Top Accomplished Women Entertainers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_(magazine)" title="Star (magazine)">Star</a></i> fabricated a story saying Witherspoon was pregnant with her third child, which led to Witherspoon suing the magazine's parent company <a href="/wiki/American_Media_(publisher)" title="American Media (publisher)">American Media Inc</a> in Los Angeles Superior Court for privacy violation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> She sought unspecified general and punitive damages in the lawsuit, asserting that the claim harmed her reputation because it suggested she was hiding the news from producers of her upcoming films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, she was selected by <i>People</i> and the entertainment news program <i><a href="/wiki/Access_Hollywood" title="Access Hollywood">Access Hollywood</a></i> as one of the year's best-dressed female stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The yellow dress she wore to that year's Golden Globe Awards was widely acclaimed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> A study conducted by E-Poll Market Research showed that Witherspoon was the most likable female celebrity of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> That same year, Witherspoon established herself as the highest-paid actress in the American film industry, earning $15 to $20 million per film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> In recent years, however, her appearance in a number of movies that fared badly at the box office caused a turnabout in her status, and she has been noted as one of the most overpaid actors in Hollywood in 2011, 2012 and 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> In April 2011, Witherspoon ranked 3rd on the 22nd annual <i>People's Most Beautiful</i> issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 1, 2010, Witherspoon received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> at 6262 Hollywood Blvd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2013, Witherspoon filed suit against Marketing Advantages International Inc., claiming it used her name and image extensively in jewelry advertising without her permission, both throughout the United States and internationally. In December 2015, while Witherspoon's trademark claims to her name were rejected, for she had not established secondary meaning to her full name, that she did not claim "emotional distress" and the "photos and facts were generally known by the public and the photos were taken in public with Plaintiff's consent", the court ruled that she could proceed with her right of publicity claims against a number of defendants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Two months later, Witherspoon withdrew her lawsuit, having "come to private agreements with the various defendants, including Centerbrook Sales, Fragrance Hut, Gemvara, and others".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Witherspoon made her second appearance among the Time 100, with her featured article being written by <a href="/wiki/Mindy_Kaling" title="Mindy Kaling">Mindy Kaling</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The same year, she was awarded, by a unanimous vote from the committee, the <a href="/wiki/American_Cinematheque" title="American Cinematheque">American Cinematheque</a> for being "a perfect example of an actress flourishing in today’s world" and "an active and successful movie producer who is moving her career forward both behind and in front of the camera".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
